            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>There are reasons Trea Turner isn't quite a 65+ future value, top-top prospect kind of prospect. He may not have any power. There are questions about his ability to make contact, or at least about his strikeout rate. There isn't really a consensus about his defense, but it's a bit telling that the Nationals chose to use him at second base last year, and there are rumors that they see him there long term. But there are reasons that Turner is very interesting in 2016, especially for fantasy purposes. He's only blocked by Stephen Drew, who has been worse than replacement for two years running now, and Danny Espinosa, who has been relegated to a backup role by his team before. Turner's contact rate was actually good in a small sample last year, too. It would have been top-20 had he qualified, and it's the kind of contact rate that Manny Machado and Jason Heyward have -- not the guys that strike out a third of the time, their contact rates are two to three times worse. Also, he has great speed and should beat his projected 20 steals if he gets the playing time. The tools are there for a good batting average with steals on the middle infield, and the opportunity is there, too. He's worth a bench pick in mixed leagues for the chance that he takes the job in spring, and a bigger investment in keeper leagues. (Eno Sarris)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>It's not impossible for Turner to some day have league average power, 25-steal type speed, and a job on the middle infield. Last year, only one middle infielder managed that feat, and although it's not great to hope for Jose Altuve all over again, it's still enough to remain interested in Turner in all leagues.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Turner sputtered in his initial call-up in 2015, but hit the ground running this year - literally. Turner swiped 33 bags in a half-season of games, while also hitting .342 with 13 homers. The speed is definitely real, and is backed up by his minor league totals and home-to-first times. Be skeptical of everything else, though. Turner never hit for that much power in college or in the minors and was given 40 future game power by scouts - the equivalent of 12 homers in a full season at peak. As a speedy, .300 hitter, Turner is an excellent fantasy second baseman. He'll likely gain shortstop eligibility this year as well, further adding to his value. But there's a decent chance Turner hits fewer homers in 2017 than he did in limited time last year. That doesn't mean you shouldn't draft him, as he's easily one of the tippy-top middle infielders in baseball. Just don't be that over-eager owner who pays for his 2016 numbers because he sees a shiny new toy. <a href="https://twitter.com/_chris_mitchell">(Chris Mitchell)</a><br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Turner established himself as an elite fantasy player in 2016, but he's due for some regression. He's a threat to steal 40+ bases, but may fall short of both .300 and 15 bombs. Still, that's phenomenal for a second baseman and/or shortstop.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
